{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_UTILIZATION_RESISTANCE", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Addressing a patient's explicit resistance to hypnosis while maintaining therapeutic rapport.", "tone_constraint": "Permissive, non-confrontational, and respectful of the patient's autonomy.", "structural_constraint": "Use of truisms, repetitive reinforcement of the word 'therapy', and the 'I don't know' technique to bypass the critical faculty."}, "instruction": "A patient states they want therapy but are strictly against the use of hypnosis. Respond to this resistance in the style of Milton Erickson, ensuring you validate their choice while subtly embedding the expectation that they will accept your therapeutic influence.", "reasoning_trace": "First, I will start with a truism: the patient is here for therapy. By stating the obvious, I gain their unconscious agreement. Second, I will use a logical bridge ('since you are coming... I expect you will take therapy') to link their physical presence to the psychological act of participation. Third, I will empower the patient by framing the therapy as something they control according to their own needs. This neutralizes the fear of being 'controlled' by hypnosis. Fourth, I will use the 'I don't know' technique. By claiming ignorance about *how* they will use the therapy, I am presupposing that they *will* use it. This shifts the focus from 'Will I accept this?' to 'How will I accept this?', which is a classic conversational trance induction technique. Finally, I will avoid the word 'hypnosis' entirely, respecting their conscious boundary while performing the work of suggestion through the repetition of 'therapeutic understandings' and 'therapeutic aid'.", "output": "You are coming for therapy, and since you are coming for therapy, I expect you will probably take therapy. And if you take therapy, it will be therapy that you take in accord with your own needs. I'll offer you the therapeutic understandings, and it is your privilege to take them in any way that you wish. I don't know—because I don't know you and I don't know your needs—I don't know exactly how you will take the therapeutic ideas, the therapeutic aid I can give you."}

He then utilizes 'physiological truisms'—suggesting the lids get heavy—which is a predictable physical response to staring, thereby establishing an unconscious 'yes-set'. The reasoning moves to 'progressive relaxation,' where he directs the subject's attention through specific body parts (feet, knees, thighs) to internalize their focus. {"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_CONGRUENCE_DIRECTIVE", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Adapting hypnotic language to the therapist's dynamic personality", "tone_constraint": "Authoritative, rhythmic, and progressively intensifying", "structural_constraint": "Repetitive phrasing with incremental adjectives to build momentum"}, "instruction": "Demonstrate how a therapist with a naturally dynamic and active personality should deliver a trance induction, focusing on congruence rather than adopting a stereotypical soft tone.", "reasoning_trace": "The objective is to show that hypnosis is most effective when the therapist's communication is congruent with their actual personality. For a dynamic person, a slow, whispering tone might feel fake and create resistance. Therefore, I will use a direct, rhythmic, and slightly authoritative command structure. I start with a personal statement of intent ('I would like you to...') which establishes the therapist's presence. This creates a rhythmic cadence that mirrors a dynamic person's natural energy while leading the subject into a deep state of focus through repetitive pacing.", "output": "I would like you to get tired... and sleepy... and sleepier... and sleepier"}

{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_LINGUISTIC_DISSOCIATION", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Linguistic depersonalization of physical pain", "tone_constraint": "Observational, analytical, and clinical", "structural_constraint": "Brief, direct illustrative quote emphasizing the shift from 'I' to 'it'"}, "instruction": "Analyze the phrase 'My finger—it hurts!' to demonstrate how patients use language to create psychological distance from physical discomfort.", "reasoning_trace": "I observe that when individuals experience intense physical discomfort, they often undergo a spontaneous hypnotic phenomenon: dissociation. In this specific utterance, the speaker begins with the possessive 'My finger,' acknowledging ownership, but immediately shifts to the third-person pronoun 'it' to describe the pain. This linguistic pivot from 'I feel pain' to 'it hurts' is a crucial psychological defense mechanism. By isolating the sensation to an externalized 'it,' the patient's core identity is protected from the suffering. I use this observation to teach that the mind is already capable of hypnotic analgesia through depersonalization. My goal in highlighting this phrase is to show how we can utilize the patient's own natural tendency to distance themselves from their body parts to facilitate deeper therapeutic trance and pain management.", "output": "My finger—it hurts!"}

It is only my joints that are bothering me."}

Freud used hypnosis for about 18 years—8 years—[until] 1896, and then Freud discovered that he could not use it for all patients. Therefore, he decided that he ought to find some method he could use for all patients. Well, that was a perfectly good idea in the early days of the development of psychiatry, but one way for all patients is a rather naive thing. But it is not to Freud’s discredit that he felt that way. [Freud] found out that he had much more interest in free association than he had in hypnosis. {"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_PHYSIOLOGICAL_PACING_AND_UTILIZATION", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Physiological pacing, ideomotor signaling, and utilization of intellectual interests during trance induction.", "tone_constraint": "Observational, permissive, authoritative yet gentle, and intellectually engaging.", "structural_constraint": "Begins with sensory pacing (eyes, pupils), transitions to ideomotor communication (nodding), introduces physiological shifts (breathing, swallowing), and concludes with the utilization of the subject's specific interest (autogenic training)."}, "instruction": "Induce a deeper trance by pacing the subject's physiological changes, establishing non-verbal communication channels, and utilizing their interest in autogenic training to frame hypnosis as a more efficient learning tool.", "reasoning_trace": "I will begin by pacing the subject's observable physiological state (pupil dilation, eye focus) to establish a 'yes-set' at the unconscious level. I will then introduce a dissociation between the mental and physical processes of eye closure to bypass conscious effort. Next, I will establish ideomotor signaling (head nodding) as a simplified communication method, which also serves to deepen the trance through repetitive, automatic movement. I will mention time distortion and respiratory changes as natural occurrences to normalize the experience. To ensure comfort, I will frame the loss of the swallowing reflex as optional and unimportant, returning control to the subject. Finally, I will utilize the subject's known interest in autogenic training, contrasting the 'slow, methodical' German approach with the 'rapid' learning possible through hypnosis, thereby creating a strong motivation for the subject to accept the hypnotic state as a superior vehicle for their existing goals.", "output": "Your pupils are dilating. There is an outer focus to your eyes, and slowly your lids are going down. You are not going to be aware of that at first. There will be a slow development within your own mind, and then perhaps there will be, first, the mental process of the eyes closing, and then there will be the physical process, and then finally there will be the physical process with the eyes remaining shut. And now you know and I know that communication can be carried on through the simple process of nodding and shaking the head. It is very easy to communicate that way. And one of the things that is characteristic of developing a trance state is the matter of the time lag. There is an alteration of the understanding of time, and so one can nod the head slowly, and keep on slowly nodding the head, without being aware of the fact that one is doing so. The respiratory movements change markedly. Your swallowing reflex is gone; you can have it back any time you want to. It is really of no importance. You can have an anesthesia, if it is important to you. I do not know if you are musically inclined, but you might like to hear music in the distance or close by, or you might want to have a tune run through your head. Or you can get back to your sleep. You might like to have a lost, lost memory come rushing into your mind with the greatest capacity for reflection. I would like to have you learn everything you can. One of the reasons I picked you out was this: I had advance knowledge that you are interested in autogenic training. I am delighted to hear that. I hope you have read Schultz and Luthe’s book with a great deal of understanding. I’d like to have you realize that that book is expressive of the slow, painstaking, methodical, all-comprehensive orientation of the German scientist. Schultz first developed autogenic training. He used the method of [inaudible] in using hypnosis, and he tried to adapt and derive understanding of what sort of psychological processes were involved [in hypnotic work] and developed autogenic training. I think the average person with autogenic training can learn in a much more rapid fashion. I think with this hypnotic knowledge, you learn all of the phases and stages of autogenesis a great deal more rapidly and comfortably."}

Ratification: I need to immediately validate Mary's admission to prevent her from retracting it. 'Now, that settles it' serves as a psychological anchor that closes the door on past doubts. 2. Linguistic Bridge: Use the conjunction 'and' to seamlessly connect the accepted fact of her ability to the next desired state, making the transition feel natural and inevitable. 3. {"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_PHYSICAL_PACING_AND_CHOICE", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Physical positioning for trance induction", "tone_constraint": "Direct, calm, and subtly permissive", "structural_constraint": "Sequence of short declarative pacing statements followed by a choice-oriented question"}, "instruction": "Provide instructions to a client to settle into their body, using physical pacing and a question that offers an illusion of choice regarding their hand position.", "reasoning_trace": "1. Establish physical grounding: I begin with simple, undeniable physical directives ('Feet on the floor') to create a 'yes-set' and focus the client's attention on their immediate bodily presence. 2. Continue pacing: I add another simple physical instruction ('Hands on your lap') to further the compliance and physical awareness without triggering conscious resistance. 3. Introduce a subtle trance-inducing question: Instead of telling the client exactly how to hold their hands, I ask a question that implies a specific, slightly unusual but relaxing posture ('hang one hand under the other'). 4. He uses a specific linguistic technique of 'stacking' adverbs ('meticulously', 'politely', 'courteously') to create a sense of heaviness and artificiality around the formal approach. This makes the audience feel the burden of such a style. He then pivots to the 'casual, personal' alternative, which functions as a reframing of what 'effective' therapy looks like. By contrasting the two, he suggests that the formal approach is actually a barrier to the unconscious rapport needed for change. The sentence is designed to make the listener question their own rigid behaviors and consider the power of a more natural, human interaction.", "output": "Now, so many of the audience members think that they must tell their patients so meticulously, so politely, so courteously exactly what to do instead of talking to them in a casual, personal,"}
{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_UTILIZATION_REFRAMING", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Resistance to hypnosis and the subject's agency in the process", "tone_constraint": "Assertive, empowering, and subtly provocative", "structural_constraint": "Direct address, rhetorical questioning, and repetitive emphasis on the subject's autonomy"}, "instruction": "내담자가 최면에 저항하며 중단을 요구하는 상황에서, 내담자의 신체적 행동을 '치료사에게 내리는 지시'로 재정의(Reframing)하여 내담자에게 통제권이 있음을 강조하고 저항을 협력으로 전환하는 에릭슨 스타일의 발화를 작성하세요.", "reasoning_trace": "먼저 내담자의 저항을 억누르려 하지 않고 오히려 '내가 시킨 것이 아님'을 명시하여 심리적 반발(Psychological Reactance)을 제거합니다. '그렇지 않습니까?'라는 수사적 질문을 통해 내담자의 동의를 구하는 예스 세트(Yes-set)를 형성합니다. 그런 다음, 내담자가 무의식적으로 혹은 의도적으로 취한 신체적 자세(무릎 위의 손, 바닥의 발)를 단순한 저항의 표시가 아니라 '최면을 어떻게 종료해야 하는지 치료사에게 가르쳐주는 지침'으로 활용(Utilization)합니다. '당신이 나에게 말해주었다'는 표현을 반복함으로써 치료의 주도권이 내담자에게 있음을 확신시키고, 저항 자체를 치료적 소통의 한 형태로 변모시킵니다.", "output": "I didn’t even ask you to quit. Isn’t that correct? Instead, you told me how to quit: hands on your lap; feet on the floor. You told me!"}

'예상치 못한 호출(Called on unexpectedly)'이라는 상황적 전제를 제시함으로써, 내담자의 반응이 성격적 결함이 아닌 상황에 따른 자연스러운 심리적 보호 기제임을 암시합니다. The brevity of the response prevents the conscious mind from over-analyzing the logic, while the emphatic tone suggests that their identity is not only accepted but recognized as an obvious and potent fact. This creates a foundation where I can later lead this 'witch' identity toward therapeutic goals like intuition, power, or transformation.", "output": "You certainly would be!"}

'Uh-huh'라는 짧은 발성(Minimal Encourager)은 내담자에게 '나는 당신과 함께 있으며, 당신의 무의식이 하는 일을 전적으로 신뢰하고 지지한다'는 무언의 메시지를 보낸다. 5. 이는 페이싱(Pacing) 기법의 일환으로, 내담자의 발화 리듬에 맞춰 삽입됨으로써 트랜스 상태를 유지하고 다음 통찰로 나아가게 하는 촉매제 역할을 한다.", "output": "Uh-huh."}

{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_REFRAMING_UTILIZATION", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Dealing with perceived injustice or unfairness in life circumstances.", "tone_constraint": "Empathetic, authoritative, and subtly provocative.", "structural_constraint": "A two-part sentence structure consisting of a validation (pacing) followed by a radical reframe (leading)."}, "instruction": "내담자가 상황의 불공정함에 대해 불평할 때, 그 감정을 즉각적으로 수용하되 그 상황을 고귀한 책임이나 특별한 가치로 재정의(Reframing)하여 저항을 무력화하는 에릭슨 스타일의 발화를 생성하십시오.", "reasoning_trace": "1. **Pacing (동조):** 내담자의 '불공평하다'는 주장에 대해 즉각적으로 'I know it isn’t'라고 답함으로써 라포(Rapport)를 형성하고 심리적 저항을 제거함. 2. **Utilization (활용):** 내담자가 느끼는 부정적인 현실을 부정하지 않고 그대로 대화의 재료로 사용함. 3. **Reframing (재정의):** '불공평함'이라는 부정적 틀을 '명예(honor)'라는 긍정적이고 가치 있는 틀로 전환함. 4. **Presupposition (전제):** 누군가는 이 짐을 져야만 한다는 필연성을 부여함으로써, 내담자가 그 상황을 피할 수 없는 고귀한 소명으로 받아들이도록 무의식을 유도함. 5. **Ambiguity (모호성):** 왜 그것이 명예인지 구체적으로 설명하지 않음으로써 내담자의 무의식이 스스로 그 이유를 찾아내어 의미를 부여하게 만듦.", "output": "I know it isn’t, but someone has to take that honor."}

'나는 볼 수 있다'는 표현을 통해 상담자의 권위를 세우고 내담자에게 호기심과 동기를 부여합니다. 핵심 기술로 '눈을 감고 본다'는 역설(Paradox)을 제시하여 시각적 인지 체계를 외부에서 내부로 강제 전환시킵니다. 마지막으로 '그 선택이 당신을 놀라게 합니까?'라는 질문을 던져, 내담자가 방법의 논리성을 따지기 전에 이미 그 방법을 선택하고 실행하고 있다는 전제를 무의식에 심어줍니다.", "output": "You are not trying hard enough, because I can see the witches there. {"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_UTILIZATION_AND_TRANSFER", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Somatic sensation transfer and utilization of muscle tension", "tone_constraint": "Observational, permissive, and inquisitive", "structural_constraint": "Utilization of paradox, pacing current experience, and indirect suggestion for physiological change"}, "instruction": "내담자가 현재 느끼고 있는 신체적 긴장이나 편안함을 활용하여, 그 감각을 신체의 다른 부위(예: 횡격막)로 전이시키도록 유도하는 에릭슨 스타일의 최면 유도문을 작성하세요. 역설적 표현과 점진적 학습의 개념을 포함해야 합니다.", "reasoning_trace": "먼저 내담자의 현재 상태를 '매우 편안함'으로 페이싱(Pacing)합니다. 그 후, 그 편안함을 유지하기 위해 근육이 사용되고 있다는 점을 '역설적 고통(agony)'으로 표현하여 신체적 긴장을 긍정적으로 활용(Utilization)합니다. 이 긴장/편안함의 에너지를 횡격막이라는 특정 부위로 전이(Transfer)할 것을 제안하며, 이를 '배워야 할 과제'로 정의하여 내담자의 무의식적 학습 동기를 자극합니다. 마지막으로 손의 움직임과 같은 이데오모터(Ideomotor) 반응을 유도하고, 열린 질문을 통해 내담자가 스스로 변화를 관찰하게 함으로써 최면적 효과를 공고히 합니다.", "output": "All right, let’s be more tangible. Have you always known that you appreciated that particular quality in a person? You are very, very comfortable now, and yet there must be some kind of agony in those muscles to hold them there comfortably. And there must be something you want to do in that very, very comfortable tightening of muscles in your arms that holds your arms comfortably. Perhaps you want to transfer that comfortable feeling to the diaphragmatic area. That is quite a job to learn, isn’t it? But you can learn it bit by bit. The right hand goes down toward your lap and ends there. Isn’t it an interesting feeling the way that tight feeling in your diaphragm [pause] is leaving? What is happening? Do you think it is working?"}

I will then detail the 'hand-lift' maneuver, explaining how a simple request for permission serves as a cover for inducing physiological catalepsy. Next, I will introduce the 'confusion technique' using meaningless pencil movements, explaining the psychological drive of the patient to project meaning onto ambiguity, which creates a vacuum for the therapist's suggestions. Finally, I will illustrate how mundane objects like microphones can be used to anchor attention and control the patient's physical orientation, concluding with a real-world observation to validate these methods.", "output": "You know, I think it is an awfully important thing for anybody who uses hypnosis to have a number of techniques that are unrecognizable to the patient. I invariably touch a patient in some way, because sometimes the patient may have had a traumatic experience that frightens them out of contact with me. Therefore, I have no hesitation about taking hold of the patient’s hand and asking: “May I lift your arm up and put it on the arm of the chair?” But by the time I get the arm up there, catalepsy is present, so I have to establish one sort of contact. Then I can very carefully, slowly move a pencil in some silly, meaningless fashion. Patients strive and struggle to put a meaning to that meaningless movement. Then later when I do the same thing, I reawaken that visual contact and they strive to put a meaning to it like before, and they reach out for any meaning I offer to them. Then, if I happen to be holding a microphone, I just automatically shift the microphone in various ways that holds their attention and causes them to shift back and forth. Mary did very, very nicely in noticing that I had done it to the other gentleman as I did with her."}
{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_CONTRAST_ANALOGY", "context_analysis": {"topic": "The distinction between laboratory psychology and clinical reality", "tone_constraint": "Authoritative, provocative, and pragmatically insightful", "structural_constraint": "Comparative structure using vivid analogies (hot stove, in vitro vs. in vivo) to lead to a clinical conclusion regarding motivation."}, "instruction": "Explain why clinical therapy must differ from laboratory psychology by emphasizing the power of single-trial learning and patient motivation, using the analogy of a hot stove and biological contexts.", "reasoning_trace": "To dismantle the rigid academic mindset of his audience, Erickson first acknowledges the standard laboratory model of conditioning (repetition). He then immediately introduces a 'shock' to that logic using a visceral, high-impact analogy—a person touching a hot stove—to prove that 'meaning' and 'survival' create instant learning (one-trial conditioning). He reinforces this by bridging to medical science (in vitro vs. in vivo), creating a hierarchy where 'living' processes are superior to 'test tube' observations. This logical progression forces the listener to realize that a patient is not a passive subject but a motivated, living organism. The final goal is to empower the therapist to stop acting like a lab technician and start utilizing the patient's internal drive as the primary tool for change.", "output": "Now, in the psychological laboratory, you learn that by combining 15 or 16 stimuli, you can build up a conditioned response. Yet you can take the primitive, naive savage who has never seen an electric stove, and you show him that red griddle on the electric stove, and he touches it just once and gets a conditioned response for the rest of his life! How many conditioned stimuli do you need? In the laboratory situation, you can get one sort of behavior; in the life situation, another sort of behavior. In medical school you learn that in vitro [in the test tube] is one sort of thing and in vivo [in the living organism] is another sort of thing. Therefore, when you are dealing with a living human being—somebody who can sit there and feel and understand—you do not treat that person as you would a culture medium that requires so many days for the culture to form. You don’t treat that patient as you would the unmotivated psychologist who is learning to develop a conditioned response. Your patient has a different kind of motivation than the volunteer subject in the psychology laboratory or the physiology laboratory. You recognize that the motivation of your patient is a tremendously important thing, and you ought to have no hesitation in bringing it about."}

{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_PRES_TRUISM", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Handedness and lateralization", "tone_constraint": "Inquisitive, gentle, and subtly disorienting", "structural_constraint": "A closed-ended question that functions as an open-ended internal search trigger"}, "instruction": "Ask the subject about their handedness in a way that bypasses conscious logic and initiates a transderivational search for internal experience.", "reasoning_trace": "To induce a light trance, I will use a presupposition that challenges the subject's static perception of their own identity. By asking 'Have you ever been...', I imply that handedness is a state that could have changed or might be temporary, which is logically absurd but psychologically provocative. Using the 'right- or left-handed' choice creates a truism—everyone falls into these categories—making the question impossible to answer with a simple 'no'. This forced choice, combined with the temporal ambiguity of 'ever been', creates a momentary cognitive 'hitch' or confusion. This confusion bypasses the critical faculty and compels the subject to look inward to verify their own history, which is the beginning of the trance state.", "output": "Have you ever been right- or left-handed?"}
{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_TRUISM", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Confirmation of physical ability (left-hand writing)", "tone_constraint": "Calm, factual, and affirming", "structural_constraint": "Short, direct declarative sentence"}, "instruction": "내담자가 이미 알고 있는 사실을 긍정하여 무의식적인 동의(Yes-set)를 이끌어내는 트루이즘(Truism) 기법을 사용하여, 왼손으로 글씨를 쓸 수 있다는 능력을 확인해 주세요.", "reasoning_trace": "먼저 내담자가 실제로 수행할 수 있는 구체적인 행동인 '왼손으로 글쓰기'를 포착합니다. 에릭슨 최면에서 이러한 명백한 사실(Truism)의 제시는 내담자의 비판적 사고를 우회하고 '예(Yes)'라는 심리적 반응을 유도하는 'Yes-set' 전략의 기초가 됩니다. 이 문장은 단순한 사실 확인을 넘어, 내담자가 자신의 신체적 통제권과 능력을 자각하게 하며 치료자와의 신뢰 관계를 공고히 합니다. 군더더기 없는 명료한 진술을 통해 내담자의 무의식이 이 제안을 저항 없이 받아들이도록 설계되었습니다.", "output": "You can write with your left hand."}
{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_UTILIZATION_FEEDBACK", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Subject's ability and self-awareness", "tone_constraint": "Non-judgmental, validating, matter-of-fact", "structural_constraint": "Direct feedback linked to previous subject input"}, "instruction": "내담자가 자신의 수행 능력이 부족하다고 느낄 때, 그 결과를 내담자가 이미 알고 있었던 사실로 돌려주어 무의식적 통찰을 강화하는 에릭슨의 대화 기법을 사용하십시오.", "reasoning_trace": "먼저 내담자의 현재 상태가 기대에 미치지 못함을 'Not too well'이라는 표현으로 가감 없이 인정하며 라포(Rapport)를 유지합니다. 이는 내담자의 현실을 있는 그대로 수용하는 페이싱(Pacing) 기법입니다. 이어지는 문구에서 'but'을 통해 반전을 꾀하며, 이 결과가 사실은 내담자가 질문을 할 당시에 이미 전달했던 정보임을 상기시킵니다. 이는 내담자의 실패를 '무의식적인 자기 인식의 정확성'으로 재프레임화(Reframing)하는 전략입니다. 내담자는 자신의 능력이 부족하다고 느끼는 대신, 자신의 무의식이 이미 상황을 정확히 꿰뚫고 있었다는 사실에 주목하게 되어 무의식에 대한 신뢰를 회복하게 됩니다.", "output": "Not too well, but you told me that when you asked the question."}

{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_IDEOMOTOR_INDUCTION", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Trance induction via ideomotor signaling and physical anchoring", "tone_constraint": "Permissive, rhythmic, observational, and subtly authoritative", "structural_constraint": "Sequential progression from sensory memory to involuntary motor response, concluding with a psychological suggestion"}, "instruction": "Guide a subject into a trance state by utilizing physical sensations and ideomotor movements, and conclude by subtly addressing their internal resistance or doubts.", "reasoning_trace": "To achieve this induction, I first establish a shared reality by referencing a physical anchor ('took hold of Mary’s hand') and asking for confirmation ('remember?'). I then use the phrase 'That’s right' to provide immediate positive reinforcement for the subject's compliance in closing their eyes. To bypass conscious resistance, I frame the involuntary movement of the hand as a sign of 'understanding' the trance state, effectively linking a physical sensation to a cognitive shift. I utilize 'pacing and leading' by narrating the small, involuntary muscle twitches ('a little jerk') as they happen, which convinces the subject that the trance is occurring naturally. By introducing a balanced motor task (left hand up, right hand down), I occupy the conscious mind with coordination, allowing me to slip in a therapeutic suggestion at the end. The final question, 'You don’t really like hanging on to those doubts, do you?', is a negative tag question designed to make the subject's unconscious mind agree to let go of skepticism without a direct confrontation.", "output": "I took hold of Mary’s hand like this, remember? And it stayed right there, and then I asked her to close her eyes. That’s right. And, now, to let me know that you are beginning to understand what it feels like to go into a trance, your left hand is slowly rising up and touching your face... .Now a littler jerk... and then another jerk... and then another .. .. and the elbow bends now. And when the left hand goes up, the right hand goes down an equal amount. You don’t really like hanging on to those doubts, do you?"}
{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_IDEOMOTOR_DISSOCIATION", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Hand movement guidance and ideomotor response", "tone_constraint": "Gentle, rhythmic, authoritative yet permissive", "structural_constraint": "Use of pacing, spatial orientation, and a paradoxical tag question"}, "instruction": "내담자의 오른손이 왼손이 있어야 할 위치로 천천히 이동하도록 유도하면서, 그 움직임이 무의식적이고 자율적인 과정임을 암시하는 최면적 언어를 사용하십시오. 특히 자신의 움직임을 스스로에게 비밀로 하기 어렵다는 역설적 표현을 포함하십시오.", "reasoning_trace": "먼저, 내담자의 현재 신체적 움직임을 있는 그대로 묘사(Pacing)하여 라포를 형성합니다. '천천히 오른손이 움직인다'는 표현은 관찰 가능한 사실을 긍정하게 만듭니다. 그 다음, '왼손이 있어야 할 곳' 혹은 '당신이 생각하는 곳'이라는 표현을 통해 실제 물리적 위치와 주관적 인지 사이의 간극을 만들어 내담자를 가벼운 혼란(Confusion) 상태로 유도합니다. 특히 몸의 '중앙선(midline)'을 넘는다는 암시는 신경학적 통합과 깊은 트랜스를 촉진하는 상징적 장치입니다. 마지막으로 '자신에게 비밀로 하기 어렵다'는 역설적 제안을 던지는데, 이는 손의 움직임이 내담자의 의식적 통제를 벗어나 자율적으로(Dissociated) 일어나고 있음을 전제합니다. '그렇지 않나요?(isn't it?)'라는 부가 의문문을 통해 내담자가 이 무의식적 현상을 거부감 없이 수용하도록 유도하며 사고의 흐름을 마무리합니다.", "output": "Slowly your right hand moves over to where your left hand should be by now... . slowly past the midline of your body to where you think your left hand should be. And it is really very hard to keep the movement of your hand secret from yourself, isn’t it?"}

{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_INTERROGATIVE_RATIFICATION", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Assessing therapeutic progress and personal agency", "tone_constraint": "Gentle, inquisitive, and subtly provocative", "structural_constraint": "A short, direct question designed to induce a transderivational search (TDS)"}, "instruction": "내담자가 자신의 변화를 인지하고 스스로의 힘으로 해냈음을 깨닫게 하기 위해, 치료자가 직접적인 도움을 주었는지 묻는 형식의 질문을 작성하십시오.", "reasoning_trace": "에릭슨은 치료의 성과를 치료자의 공으로 돌리기보다 내담자의 무의식적 성취로 돌리는 것을 선호한다. 이 질문은 표면적으로는 치료자의 기여도를 묻는 것처럼 보이지만, 실제로는 내담자가 자신의 내면을 탐색(Transderivational Search)하게 하여 '무엇이 변했는가'를 스스로 확인하게 만든다. What is happening?"}

{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_PHYSIOLOGICAL_PACING", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Physiological indicators of trance and the resulting loss of self-consciousness.", "tone_constraint": "Clinical, observational, authoritative, yet hypnotically rhythmic.", "structural_constraint": "A series of rhetorical questions followed by a catalog of physiological changes, concluding with a definitive statement of psychological shift."}, "instruction": "Describe the physiological changes of a subject in a deep trance to an audience, emphasizing the loss of self-consciousness through detailed observation of physical immobility and autonomic changes.", "reasoning_trace": "To achieve the desired effect, I first engage the audience's visual perception using rhetorical questions ('Did you watch...', 'Did you notice...'), which serves to validate the subject's state through external evidence. I then systematically catalog specific physiological markers—the 'ironing out' of facial expressions, the restriction of movement to the eyes, the loss of mobility in the mouth, cheeks, and hands, and changes in autonomic functions like respiration and swallowing. This detailed pacing of observable reality builds an undeniable case for the depth of the trance. By contrasting this state with her previous 'self-conscious responses,' I highlight the psychological shift. Finally, I introduce a paradoxical suggestion: she hears everything, yet the self-consciousness has disappeared, concluding with a powerful truism ('It is true') to solidify the suggestion of her freedom from social anxiety.", "output": "Did you watch her face and notice that there has been an ironing out of her facial expression? Did you notice that her expression tends to limit itself to the eyes entirely; that she is keeping a very rapid movement of her eyes; that her mouth has lost a lot of its mobility; that her cheeks have lost a lot of their mobility? She has lost the mobility of her hands; there has been a change in her respiratory rhythm; there has been a change in her swallowing reflex; there has been a change in the mobility of her head. And even though I am talking about her to the audience, there hasn’t been the self-conscious responses that she made previously. And I am still talking about her, and she hears everything I say, but in some peculiar way, the self-consciousness has disappeared. It is true. She is free of her self-consciousness from the audience."}
{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_TRUISM_UNCONSCIOUS_AWARENESS", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Handedness and the gap between conscious awareness and unconscious behavior", "tone_constraint": "Observational, rhythmic, and subtly provocative to shift focus toward the unconscious.", "structural_constraint": "Repetition of a simple truth (truism) followed by a contrasting observation using a conjunction like 'and yet'."}, "instruction": "내담자가 평소 의식하지 못했던 자동적인 행동(오른손잡이/왼손잡이 습관)을 언급하며, 의식적인 자각 없이도 무의식은 이미 정보를 처리하고 표현하고 있었다는 사실을 깨닫게 유도하는 최면적 발화를 작성하십시오.", "reasoning_trace": "먼저 내담자가 자신의 신체적 습관에 대해 깊게 생각해보지 않았다는 '자명한 사실(Truism)'을 제시하여 저항을 줄입니다. 동일한 문장('You never thought about it')을 반복함으로써 내담자의 주의를 내면으로 고정시키고 리듬감을 형성합니다. 그 다음, 'and yet(그런데도)'이라는 연결어를 사용하여 의식의 부재와 무의식적 표출 사이의 대조를 만듭니다. 이는 내담자로 하여금 '내가 의식하지 못하는 사이에도 내 몸과 무의식은 이미 소통하고 있었구나'라는 통찰을 얻게 하며, 무의식적 자원과의 연결을 강화하는 효과를 의도한 것입니다.", "output": "You never thought about it. You never thought about it, and yet you spoke about it here."}
{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_PACING_LEADING", "context_analysis": {"topic": "The return of a specific internal sensation or feeling", "tone_constraint": "Observational, gentle, and subtly authoritative", "structural_constraint": "Validation statement followed by a temporal anchor and a tag question"}, "instruction": "내담자가 이전에 경험했던 특정한 감각이나 감정이 현재 시점에서 다시 살아나고 있음을 암시하고, 이를 확증하기 위한 에릭슨 스타일의 유도 문장을 작성하십시오.", "reasoning_trace": "먼저 'I know what you mean'이라는 표현을 통해 내담자의 주관적 경험에 공감하며 라포(Rapport)를 형성합니다. 이는 내담자의 세계관에 치료자가 동조하고 있음을 알리는 페이싱(Pacing) 단계입니다. 그 다음 'now'라는 단어를 두 번 반복 사용하여 내담자의 주의를 '현재'의 신체적 감각으로 강력하게 고정시킵니다. 'and'라는 연결어는 치료자의 이해와 내담자의 현상적 변화를 인과적으로 연결하는 가교 역할을 합니다. 마지막으로 'isn't it?'이라는 부가 의무문(Tag Question)을 사용하여 내담자가 자신의 내부를 탐색하고 그 감각의 귀환을 스스로 긍정하게 유도(Leading)합니다. 이는 내담자의 무의식적 동의를 이끌어내는 전형적인 최면적 기법입니다.", "output": "I know what you mean now, and now that feeling is coming back, isn’t it?"}
{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_PRESUPPOSITION_PROCESS", "context_analysis": {"topic": "The return of sensation or awareness after a hypnotic state.", "tone_constraint": "Curious, minimalist, and non-directive yet leading.", "structural_constraint": "A short, open-ended question focusing on the 'how' rather than the 'if'."}, "instruction": "내담자가 최면적 무감각이나 특정 상태에서 벗어나 감각이 회복되는 순간, 그 회복의 '사실'을 전제하면서 회복의 '과정'에 집중하게 만드는 질문을 하십시오.", "reasoning_trace": "첫째, 내담자의 감각이 돌아왔는지 여부를 묻는 '예/아니오' 질문은 불확실성을 유발할 수 있으므로 피한다. 둘째, 'How(어떻게)'라는 의문사를 사용하여 감각이 이미 돌아왔음을 강력하게 전제(Presupposition)한다. 셋째, 내담자가 자신의 내부 감각 변화 과정을 스스로 추적하게 함으로써, 무의식적 반응을 의식화하고 그 변화를 자신의 것으로 수용(Integration)하게 만든다. 넷째, 'come back to you'라는 표현을 통해 감각의 회복이 외부의 강요가 아닌 자연스러운 귀환임을 암시한다.", "output": "How did it come back to you?"}
{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_UNCONSCIOUS_AUTONOMY", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Acknowledging the autonomous return of a state or memory", "tone_constraint": "Permissive, validating, and subtly authoritative", "structural_constraint": "Short, direct statement focusing on the limitation of conscious knowledge"}, "instruction": "내담자가 무의식적인 반응이나 기억의 회복을 경험했을 때, 그 과정이 의식의 통제나 이해를 벗어나 일어났음을 긍정함으로써 무의식의 자율적 능력을 강화하는 에릭슨 스타일의 문장을 생성하십시오.", "reasoning_trace": "먼저 내담자가 방금 경험한 현상(무언가가 돌아온 것)을 인정한다. 에릭슨의 핵심 전략은 '의식'과 '무의식'을 분리하는 것이다. 'You don’t know'라는 표현을 통해 의식적인 분석의 필요성을 제거하고, 그 현상이 무의식의 영역에서 스스로 일어났음을 암시한다. 이는 내담자가 자신의 무의식을 신뢰하게 만들며, '어떻게(how)' 돌아왔는지 모른다는 사실 자체를 긍정적인 신호로 전환시킨다. 또한 'it came back'이라는 표현은 이미 회복이나 변화가 성공적으로 이루어졌음을 전제로 하는 강력한 전제(Presupposition)를 담고 있다.", "output": "You don’t know how it came back."}
{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_PRESENSORY_LEAD", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Physical touch and comfort induction", "tone_constraint": "Gentle, reassuring, and authoritative", "structural_constraint": "Past-to-present transition with presuppositional questioning"}, "instruction": "내담자의 이마를 만진 후, 그 행위가 안전했음을 인지시키고 현재의 편안한 감각에 집중하도록 유도하는 에릭슨 스타일의 대화를 생성하라.", "reasoning_trace": "먼저 '더 이상 필요하지 않다'는 표현을 통해 과거의 긴장이나 불필요한 상태로부터 내담자를 분리시키는 암시를 제공한다. 그 다음, 실제 발생한 물리적 접촉(이마를 만짐)을 객관적 사실로 언급하여 내담자의 현재 경험을 치료자의 언어와 일치시킨다. 치료자가 '매우 조심스러웠음'을 강조하는 것은 무의식적 저항을 줄이고 신뢰 관계(Rapport)를 강화하는 장치이다. 마지막으로 '이제(Now)'라는 시간적 전환어를 사용하여 주의를 현재의 감각으로 돌린 뒤, '편안함'이라는 상태를 전제한 질문('느껴지나요?')을 던짐으로써 내담자가 자신의 내부에서 긍정적인 감각을 스스로 찾아내고 확증하도록 유도한다.", "output": "You didn’t need it anymore. I touched your forehead. I was very careful about that. Now, do you notice that that feeling is comfortable?"}
{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_UNCONSCIOUS_ASSOCIATION", "context_analysis": {"topic": "The strategic linking of suppressed past traits to current behavioral goals and the validation of unconscious curiosity.", "tone_constraint": "Authoritative, mysterious, yet deeply validating and pedagogical.", "structural_constraint": "A narrative explanation that bridges conscious ignorance with unconscious understanding, using simple metaphors like 'tying together'."}, "instruction": "Explain the psychological rationale behind linking a subject's suppressed left-handedness to their desire to sing, while addressing an observer's question about the process in a way that reinforces the power of the unconscious mind.", "reasoning_trace": "First, I must validate the observer's inquiry to encourage their own unconscious learning process, labeling their question as 'highly important.' Next, I will reveal the 'accidental' discovery of a suppressed resource—Mary's original left-handedness—which represents a part of her identity that was 'deprived.' By framing the intervention as a simple act of 'tying the two together,' I demystify the technique while maintaining its potency. I must emphasize that this connection was invisible to the conscious mind ('She couldn’t see me tie it'), which highlights the bypass of conscious resistance. Finally, I will create a paradoxical loop: the observer's unconscious understood the association well enough to prompt the question, even if their conscious mind remains confused. This reinforces the idea that the unconscious is always a step ahead in perceiving therapeutic structures.", "output": "The question that you asked is so important. I got the accidental information from Mary that once she was left-handed. For a long time, Mary has wanted to sing in public. Long ago she was deprived of something—left-handed writing—so I simply tied the two together. It was so easily done, for she could write that letter with her left hand, and it is tied to singing. She couldn’t see me tie it to the singing, and neither could anybody else. But I tied the two together, and I am not the least bit afraid of telling Mary. Your unconscious didn’t understand that [association], and yet your unconscious understood it well enough to ask me that highly important question."}
{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_PRESUPPOSITION_LINKING", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Trance induction through cognitive linking and temporal presupposition", "tone_constraint": "Inquisitive, validating, and subtly directive", "structural_constraint": "Rhetorical opening, validation of conscious perception, and a double-bind presupposition"}, "instruction": "내담자가 과거의 경험들 사이의 연결고리를 의식적으로 인식하게 한 뒤, 이를 바탕으로 트랜스 진입 시점을 선택하게 하는 전제 기법을 사용하여 발화하세요.", "reasoning_trace": "먼저 '내가 어떻게 했는가?'라는 질문을 던져 내담자의 주의를 분석적인 모드에서 관찰적인 모드로 전환시킵니다. 이어서 내담자가 의식적으로 파악한 논리적 연결(왼손 글쓰기와 노래의 상관관계)을 언급함으로써, 내담자의 의식적 노력을 인정하고 라포(Rapport)를 강화합니다. 이는 '의식'을 바쁘게 만들어 무의식의 문을 여는 전략입니다. 마지막으로 '이제(Now)'라는 단어로 현재의 결정을 촉구하며, '언제 트랜스에 들어가고 싶은가?'라는 질문을 통해 트랜스 진입 여부가 아닌 '시기'에만 집중하게 만드는 강력한 전제(Presupposition)를 사용합니다. '정말로(really)'라는 수식어는 내담자의 내면적 욕구를 자극하여 저항 없이 트랜스를 수용하게 만듭니다.", "output": "How did | do it? I observe the physiological markers of anger (breathing, muscle tension, flushing) and offer a simple linguistic label. This directness serves two purposes: first, it brings the unconscious affect into conscious awareness; second, it forces the patient to either validate their experience or provide a correction, both of which provide more 'material' for the hypnotic work. '우리(we)'라는 표현을 통해 고통을 보편적인 인간의 경험으로 일반화합니다. 둘째, 'self-conscious'와 'pain/distress'를 연결하여 자의식이 고통의 원인이 될 수 있음을 암시적으로 수용하게 합니다. 셋째, 'How is your...?'라는 질문을 통해 내담자가 자신의 고통을 분석하거나 정당화하는 대신, 그 고통의 '상태'나 '성질'을 객관적으로 묘사하도록 유도합니다. 이는 내담자를 고통으로부터 분리(Dissociation)시키는 효과를 줍니다.", "output": "Sometimes when we are self-conscious, we are in pain or distress. How is your self-conscious distress?"}

{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_REFRAMING_AND_RHETORICAL_QUESTION", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Overcoming resistance in a therapeutic setting", "tone_constraint": "Authoritative, strategic, and psychologically provocative", "structural_constraint": "A declarative statement of action followed by a rhetorical, presuppositional question"}, "instruction": "내담자의 저항을 직면했을 때, 이를 부정적인 장애물이 아닌 '학습의 과정'으로 재정의(Reframing)하고, 수사적 질문을 던져 내담자의 무의식이 저항을 극복하는 것 외에 다른 대안이 없음을 스스로 깨닫게 만드는 에릭슨 스타일의 발화를 작성하십시오.", "reasoning_trace": "먼저, 내담자가 느끼는 '저항'이라는 부정적 상태를 '학습 상황(learning situation)'이라는 긍정적이고 생산적인 프레임으로 전환합니다. 이는 내담자의 방어 기제를 무력화시키고 현재의 불편함을 성장을 위한 필수 단계로 인식하게 만듭니다. 그 다음, '그 외에 어떻게 저항을 극복하겠는가?'라는 수사적 질문을 던집니다. 이 질문은 내담자의 의식적인 논리를 우회하여, 현재의 상황(학습)이 저항을 해결할 수 있는 유일하거나 가장 타당한 방법이라는 전제를 무의식에 심어줍니다. 질문의 형식을 빌렸지만 실제로는 '이것이 유일한 길이다'라는 강력한 암시를 전달하는 전략적 모호성을 활용한 것입니다.", "output": "I put you in a learning situation. How else does one overcome resistance?"}
{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_PRESUPPOSITION", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Awareness of the external environment during a therapeutic interaction", "tone_constraint": "Inquisitive, gentle, and subtly authoritative through linguistic presupposition", "structural_constraint": "An open-ended question starting with 'how many times' to bypass conscious resistance"}, "instruction": "내담자가 대화에 깊이 몰입하여 주변 환경(청중)을 의식하지 못했다는 사실을 당연한 전제로 깔고, 그 횟수를 묻는 방식으로 무의식적 트랜스 상태를 확인하고 강화하십시오.", "reasoning_trace": "1. 내담자의 현재 상태를 진단하기 위해 '청중의 존재'라는 외부 자극에 대한 인지 정도를 확인하고자 함. 2. '청중을 잊었습니까?'라는 폐쇄형 질문은 내담자의 의식적인 검열을 유도하여 '아니오'라는 부정적 답변을 이끌어낼 위험이 있음. 3. 이를 피하기 위해 '얼마나 자주(how many times)'라는 수량적 질문 형식을 취함. 4. 이 질문은 내담자가 이미 청중을 잊었다는 사실을 전제(Presupposition)로 포함하고 있음. 5. 내담자는 질문에 답하기 위해 자신의 기억을 검색하는 과정에서 실제로 청중을 잊었던 무의식적 순간들을 재경험하게 되며, 이는 결과적으로 현재의 몰입 상태를 더욱 심화시키는 암시로 작용함.", "output": "While we were talking here, how many times have you forgotten the presence of the audience?"}
{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_PRECISION_INQUIRY", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Quantifying subjective experience or behavior", "tone_constraint": "Persistent, probing, and clinically curious", "structural_constraint": "Short, direct interrogative with a trailing emphasis"}, "instruction": "내담자가 자신의 행동이나 증상의 빈도를 모호하게 넘어가지 못하도록, 무의식적인 탐색과 구체적인 직면을 유도하는 밀턴 에릭슨의 압박 질문을 작성하세요.", "reasoning_trace": "에릭슨은 내담자의 모호한 일반화(Generalization)를 깨뜨리기 위해 의도적으로 구체적인 수치를 요구하는 전략을 사용합니다. 'How many times'라는 질문은 내담자의 의식적인 마음이 논리적이고 구체적인 데이터를 찾기 위해 내부 검색을 수행하게 만듭니다. 이 과정에서 내담자는 일시적인 트랜스 상태에 진입하거나 자신의 패턴을 객관적으로 바라보게 됩니다. 특히 문장 끝에 'though'를 덧붙임으로써, 이전의 대화 흐름을 차단하고 현재의 질문에 강력한 주의(Attention)를 고정시키며 대답을 유도하는 심리적 압박을 완성합니다.", "output": "How many times, though?"}
{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_PACING_LEADING", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Transitioning from deep focus to external awareness", "tone_constraint": "Gentle, validating, and subtly authoritative", "structural_constraint": "Summary of subjective experience followed by a tag question and a re-orienting inquiry"}, "instruction": "내담자가 치료적 트랜스 상태에서 외부 환경으로 주의를 돌리기 시작할 때, 그들의 몰입 상태를 긍정적으로 정의하고 자연스럽게 현실로 복귀하도록 유도하는 에릭슨 스타일의 발화를 작성하십시오.", "reasoning_trace": "먼저 내담자의 현재 상태(자아 의식의 상실 및 치료자에게의 집중)를 'In other words'라는 표현을 통해 명확하게 요약하여 페이싱(Pacing)합니다. 이는 내담자가 겪은 주관적 경험에 논리적 틀을 부여합니다. 그 후 'Isn’t that right?'라는 부가 의문문을 사용하여 내담자의 무의식적 동의를 이끌어내는 'Yes-set'을 형성합니다. 마지막으로, 청중(외부 세계)과의 접촉을 언급하며 주의를 내부에서 외부로 부드럽게 이동시키는 리딩(Leading) 기법을 적용합니다. 'How does it feel'이라는 개방형 질문은 내담자가 자신의 변화된 상태를 스스로 관찰하고 통합하게 만듭니다.", "output": "In other words, you have lost your self-consciousness so much that you were just paying attention to me. Isn’t that right? How does it feel to come back in contact with the audience?"}
{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_MINIMAL_SUGGESTION_AUTONOMY", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Physical touch and patient autonomy in hypnotic suggestion", "tone_constraint": "Instructive, observant, and subtly authoritative", "structural_constraint": "Parallelism between physical movement and psychological state (anesthesia)"}, "instruction": "내담자의 신체적 움직임과 마취 현상을 유도할 때, 치료자의 개입을 최소화하고 내담자의 자율성을 극대화하는 에릭슨의 접근 방식을 설명하고 시연하십시오.", "reasoning_trace": "먼저 내담자의 주의를 자신의 행동에 대한 걱정에서 치료자와의 상호작용으로 돌립니다. '어떻게 느껴지는가'와 같은 개방형 질문을 통해 내담자가 자신의 감각에 집중하게 만듭니다. 그 후, 치료자의 역할은 단지 '방향을 제시'하는 것일 뿐, 실제 움직임이나 마취와 같은 심리적 변화는 내담자 스스로가 만들어내는 것임을 강조합니다. '가벼운 터치'와 '실제로 들어 올리지 않음'이라는 물리적 비유를 사용하여, 최면적 암시가 강요가 아닌 제안임을 명시합니다. 마지막으로 마취(anesthesia)라는 구체적인 현상을 예로 들어, 모든 치유와 변화의 주체는 내담자임을 확립합니다.", "output": "You are not concerned about your actions. You are more concerned about them. How does it feel when I take hold of your wrists? In what way do I jar them up? You suggest it by a slight movement, by a light touch, by not actually lifting them. That is an awfully important thing for the audience members to bear in mind. You touch, you suggest the direction of the movement. You leave the movement to the patient. You suggest the anesthesia to the patient, but you leave the anesthesia to the patient—just as Mary produced her own anesthesia."}
{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_ANALOGY_UTILIZATION", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Physiological effects of spinal anesthesia as a bridge to hypnotic trance", "tone_constraint": "Clinical, matter-of-fact, yet subtly suggestive and authoritative.", "structural_constraint": "Begins with a rhetorical medical question, describes physical dissociation, and uses a conjunction to bridge to a direct hypnotic suggestion."}, "instruction": "Describe the physical sensations of spinal anesthesia to a patient or student, and then use that description as a metaphor to transition into a discussion about the duration of their hypnotic trance.", "reasoning_trace": "1. Establish a physiological baseline: Start with a medical reality (local spinal anesthesia) that the subject can intellectually accept as a fact. 2. Mirror hypnotic phenomena: Describe the effects of the spinal in terms that parallel hypnotic states—reduced activity, loss of sensation, and functional catalepsy. 3. Distinguish functional from organic: Use the phrase 'though they are not truly paralyzed' to reassure the unconscious mind that this state is temporary and safe, much like a trance. 4. Bypass conscious will: Emphasize the loss of voluntary control ('don't know how to move') to suggest that movement is a learned conscious behavior that can be suspended. 5. The Bridge: Use the conjunction 'And' to seamlessly link the medical description to the hypnotic context. 6. Presupposition: Conclude with an open-ended question about the duration of the trance, which presupposes that the trance is already occurring or inevitable, shifting the focus from 'if' to 'how long'.", "output": "What does a local spinal do to patients? It lessens their activity. They lose their sensation; they don’t know how to move their legs. They become paralyzed, though they are not truly paralyzed. They have no feeling. Then, I transition into the 'definition' phase where I take control of the subject's perception. I use the word 'defined' to signal that reality is a construct I am currently shaping. By repeating 'nice, big room' and 'large room', I bypass critical resistance through simple, positive affirmations. The core of the technique lies in the spatial anchors: using 'way back there' and 'way over there' forces the subject's internal representation to expand. By directing their gaze (and thus their mind) to distant points, I physically and mentally stretch the boundaries of their perceived environment, replacing the sensation of being 'trapped' with the active process of 'looking across a vast distance'.", "output": "Right—claustrophobia. {"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_UTILIZATION_REFRAMING", "context_analysis": {"topic": "The therapeutic function and normalization of patient resistance", "tone_constraint": "Permissive, paradoxically logical, and de-escalating", "structural_constraint": "Use of rhetorical questions, validation of the patient's perspective, and reframing a 'problem' as a 'justified symptom'"}, "instruction": "Explain why patient resistance should be met with humor and respect rather than being treated as a serious obstacle, while justifying the patient's right to resist.", "reasoning_trace": "First, I will challenge the conventional view of resistance as a 'serious problem' by using rhetorical questions to introduce humor as a viable alternative. Second, I will validate the patient's internal logic: they are being asked to change by a stranger who claims to understand them better than they understand themselves, which naturally triggers a self-protective response. Third, I will utilize the concept of 'truisms' to establish that resistance is not only expected but 'justified' and 'ought' to happen. By framing resistance as a necessary part of their symptomatology, I am effectively utilizing the resistance rather than fighting it. Finally, I will conclude that by respecting this resistance and giving it a 'rightful place' in therapy, the therapist gains the flexibility to work with the patient's existing psychological structure instead of against it.", "output": "Instead of treating that resistance seriously, as if it were a desperately serious problem that had to be dealt with, why shouldn’t I laugh about it? Why shouldn’t the patient laugh about it? No reason at all, because patients really ought to show some resistance to you. They come to you, and they know that you are going to change them in some way, but they don’t know how. They have no idea of how thoroughly you understand their problems; but they know very well that they don’t understand their problems, so how could a perfect stranger understand them? They are justified in having resistance. Therefore, they ought to show that resistance as a part of their symptomatology, and the therapist ought to respect it, but he also ought to put it in its rightful place in a therapeutic situation."}
{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_PRESUPPOSITION_DOUBLE_BIND", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Comfort level in physical environments", "tone_constraint": "Gentle, inquisitive, and subtly directive", "structural_constraint": "A choice between two polar opposites that both presuppose a specific internal state (comfort)."}, "instruction": "내담자가 특정 환경에서 '편안함'을 느끼는 것을 당연한 전제로 받아들이게 하면서, 그 범위를 스스로 탐색하도록 유도하는 이중 구속(Double Bind) 질문을 작성하십시오.", "reasoning_trace": "먼저, 내담자의 의식적인 초점을 '방의 크기'라는 외부적인 척도로 돌립니다. '당신은 ~하고 싶지 않겠죠?'라는 형식은 내담자가 즉각적으로 '아니오'라고 답하더라도 결과적으로 상담자의 진술에 동의하게 만드는 심리적 효과가 있음. 둘째, '식당의 구석진 자리'라는 구체적인 공간적 이미지를 제시하여 내담자가 머릿속으로 그 상황을 시뮬레이션하도록 유도함. 이는 가벼운 트랜스 상태를 유발하는 기법임. 셋째, 문장 끝에 '그렇죠?(would you?)'라는 부가 의문문을 붙임으로써, 내담자가 자신의 내면을 확인하고 반응을 보이도록 부드럽게 압박함. 이 과정에서 내담자가 보이는 미세한 표정 변화나 망설임은 그의 대인관계적 성향이나 안전에 대한 욕구를 파악하는 단서가 됨.", "output": "You wouldn’t want to sit in the far corner of a restaurant, would you?"}
{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_TRUISM_AMBIGUITY", "context_analysis": {"topic": "The subject's fluctuating feelings about sitting in a restaurant", "tone_constraint": "Calm, non-judgmental, and subtly provocative", "structural_constraint": "Brief, rhythmic contrast using universal quantifiers"}, "instruction": "밀턴 에릭슨의 대화형 최면 기법을 사용하여, 내담자가 특정 상황(식당)에서 느끼는 감정의 가변성을 인정하고 그 원인을 무의식적으로 탐색하게 만드는 질문을 하세요. 보편적 진실(Truism)을 활용하여 저항을 최소화하십시오.", "reasoning_trace": "먼저, 'Sometimes you would and sometimes you wouldn’t'이라는 문장은 부정할 수 없는 보편적 진실(Truism)입니다. 인간의 감정은 가변적이기 때문에 내담자는 이 진술을 즉각적으로 수용하게 되며, 이는 치료자와의 라포(Rapport)를 강화하고 비판적 사고를 우회합니다. Why?"}

{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_REFRAMING_UTILIZATION", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Redefining the nature of a psychological problem through the subject's own report", "tone_constraint": "Observational, respectful, and insightfully authoritative", "structural_constraint": "Rhetorical question followed by a reinterpretation of the subject's description to highlight variability"}, "instruction": "내담자가 자신의 문제를 고정된 것으로 인식하지 않도록, 내담자의 말을 활용하여 문제의 가변성을 강조하는 밀턴 에릭슨의 방식으로 설명해 주세요.", "reasoning_trace": "먼저, 내담자가 제공한 정보를 수동적으로 수용하는 것이 아니라 치료적 자산으로 활용(Utilization)하기 위해 수사적 질문을 던집니다. 내담자는 자신의 증상을 고통스럽게 호소했을 수 있지만, 에릭슨은 이를 '나에게 정보를 친절하게 알려주었다'고 재정의(Reframing)하여 내담자의 협력을 이끌어냅니다. 핵심은 내담자가 자신의 문제를 '고정되고 해결 불가능한 것(fixed and rigid and insoluble)'으로 보지 않도록 만드는 것입니다. 이를 위해 내담자의 말 속에 숨겨진 '예외 상황(신경이 괜찮을 때)'을 포착하여 강조합니다. 증상이 나타나지 않는 순간이 있다는 사실을 부각함으로써, 문제가 가변적이며 따라서 변화와 치유가 가능하다는 무의식적 암시를 심어줍니다.", "output": "What information has the subject given me? He has already told me very nicely, in his own words, that his problem is not a fixed and rigid and insoluble problem; that there are times when his nerves are alright, and times when his nerves are not alright."}

{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_UTILIZATION_OF_NONVERBAL", "context_analysis": {"topic": "The inability to verbalize the subjective experience of relaxation.", "tone_constraint": "Permissive, validating, and observant.", "structural_constraint": "Begins with a truism about verbal limitations, followed by an observation of physical behavior as a form of unconscious communication."}, "instruction": "Create a response that validates a subject's difficulty in explaining their internal state of relaxation, then redirect their attention to their involuntary physical movements as a more authentic form of communication.", "reasoning_trace": "1. Acknowledge the limitation: Start by agreeing with the subject's inability to explain relaxation. This functions as a truism—it is indeed difficult to put subjective feelings into words. This reduces conscious performance anxiety. 2. Shift the focus: Move the emphasis from conscious verbalization to unconscious physical expression. 3. Utilize non-verbal cues: Identify specific physical actions (crossing legs, touching) that the subject performed unconsciously. 4. Reframing: Frame these movements not as random acts, but as a 'showing' or a demonstration of the state they couldn't describe. 5. Reinforcement: Use 'Thanks for showing me' to reward the unconscious mind for its communication, bypassing the conscious mind's struggle to find the right words.", "output": "You can’t really explain it. Thanks for showing me —you crossed your legs and touched yourself."}
{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_YES_SET_VALIDATION", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Validation of the subject's relaxation state", "tone_constraint": "Calm, authoritative, and reinforcing", "structural_constraint": "Brief, direct affirmation used as a pacing mechanism"}, "instruction": "내담자가 자신의 이완 상태를 표현했을 때, 이를 즉각적으로 긍정하여 라포를 형성하고 무의식적인 수용 상태(Yes Set)를 강화하는 에릭슨의 발화를 작성하십시오.", "reasoning_trace": "에릭슨의 치료적 의사소통에서 'That's right'는 단순한 동의 이상의 의미를 갖습니다. 첫째, 내담자의 현재 주관적 경험(이완)을 외부의 권위(치료자)가 공식적으로 인정함으로써 내담자의 자아를 안심시킵니다. 둘째, 'Yes Set' 기법의 일환으로, 내담자가 자신의 경험이 옳다는 것을 반복적으로 확인하게 하여 이후에 이어질 치료적 암시를 비판 없이 수용하도록 유도합니다. 셋째, 이 짧은 문장은 내담자의 내부 집중을 방해하지 않으면서도 치료자가 함께하고 있다는 강력한 현존감을 전달합니다. 이는 내담자가 자신의 무의식적 반응을 신뢰하도록 만드는 핵심적인 페이싱(Pacing) 전략입니다.", "output": "That's right."}
{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_UTILIZATION_AGREEMENT", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Establishing a safe therapeutic environment through mutual protection", "tone_constraint": "Calm, reassuring, and collaborative", "structural_constraint": "Short, affirmative, and inclusive sentence structure"}, "instruction": "내담자가 자신의 심리적 상태나 현재의 치료적 상황을 보호받고 싶어 하는 욕구를 보일 때, 이를 전적으로 수용하고 협력적인 동맹을 강화하는 밀턴 에릭슨의 어조로 응답하십시오.", "reasoning_trace": "먼저 'Yes'라는 단어를 통해 내담자의 현재 상태나 제안을 즉각적으로 긍정하며 '예스 세트(Yes-set)'를 형성합니다. 이는 내담자의 저항을 줄이고 라포를 강화하는 기초가 됩니다. 그 다음 'Let’s'라는 제안형 우리(we) 화법을 사용하여 치료자와 내담자가 분리된 존재가 아닌, 공동의 목표를 가진 파트너임을 암시합니다. 'Protect the situation'이라는 표현은 구체적으로 무엇을 보호할지 명시하지 않음으로써 내담자의 무의식이 스스로 가장 보호가 필요한 영역(비밀, 상처, 혹은 변화의 속도 등)을 투사하도록 유도합니다. 이는 내담자에게 통제권을 부여하면서도 치료자가 그 울타리가 되어줄 것임을 확신시키는 고도로 계산된 단순성입니다.", "output": "Yes. Let’s protect the situation."}
{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_MULTI_LEVEL_COMMUNICATION", "context_analysis": {"topic": "The distinction between conscious and unconscious communication through behavioral observation.", "tone_constraint": "Didactic, observational, and subtly authoritative.", "structural_constraint": "Anecdotal evidence followed by a theoretical synthesis."}, "instruction": "Describe how you utilize a simple question to elicit an unconscious physical response and how you acknowledge that response to demonstrate two-level communication.", "reasoning_trace": "To illustrate the concept of multi-level communication, I must first create a scenario where the conscious mind is occupied with a question while the unconscious mind provides the real answer through behavior. I choose the topic of 'relaxation' because it is inherently experiential. By asking 'How do you relax?', I am not seeking a verbal description; I am prompting the patient's body to search for and manifest that state. When the patient shifts their posture or breathing—the actual act of relaxing—I immediately acknowledge this non-verbal 'showing' with a 'Thank you.' This bypasses the verbal content and targets the behavioral reality. Finally, I explicitly define this for the observer as the split between conscious inquiry and unconscious demonstration, reinforcing the therapist's need to attend to what is 'shown' rather than just what is 'said'.", "output": "I said, \"Thanks for showing me.\" I asked him first, \"How do you relax?\" Well, how was he sitting? I asked him, \"How do you relax?\", and then I thanked him for showing me. That is communication at two different levels—communication at the conscious level and communication at the unconscious level."}
{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_PRESUPPOSITION_QUANTITY", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Assessing the subject's expectations for hypnotic intervention regarding phobias.", "tone_constraint": "Permissive yet authoritative, utilizing presuppositional questioning.", "structural_constraint": "An open-ended question that embeds a presupposition of success and utilizes negative affect toward the symptom."}, "instruction": "Ask the subject how much hypnosis they believe is necessary to overcome their fear and claustrophobia, framing the question to presuppose that success is inevitable and that the symptoms are inherently repulsive.", "reasoning_trace": "To construct this intervention, I first identify the core issue: fear and claustrophobia. I want to bypass the subject's skepticism about whether hypnosis will work. Therefore, I use a presupposition of quantity ('How much...'), which forces the conscious mind to focus on the duration or intensity of the process rather than the possibility of failure. I then utilize the subject's own negative experience by labeling the symptoms as 'disgusting qualities,' which helps the subject mentally distance themselves from the phobia and increases the drive toward 'freedom.' By asking 'do you think you'll need,' I am empowering the subject's unconscious mind to set its own pace for recovery, thereby increasing their commitment to the therapeutic outcome.", "output": "How much hypnosis do you think you'll need to achieve a freedom from the disgusting qualities of fear and of claustrophobia?"}

'I think you're right'라는 표현은 내담자의 예상을 뛰어넘는 역설적 개입으로, 상담자와의 대립 구도를 해체한다. 마지막으로, 상담자가 겪을 어려움에 대한 논의를 내담자가 스스로 해결해야 할 과제나 직면해야 할 문제의 정도로 치환하여 질문함으로써, 내담자의 무의식이 자신의 문제를 탐색하도록 유도한다. 이는 투사된 저항을 내면의 성찰로 되돌리는 고도의 전략적 전환이다.", "output": "All right. Wouldn’t it be much better to get over fighting it?"}

{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_SHOCK_AND_DISPLACEMENT", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Treating elevator phobia through a staged social ordeal and pattern interruption.", "tone_constraint": "Narrative, provocative, authoritative, and experiential.", "structural_constraint": "Anecdotal storytelling used to illustrate a psychological shift from fear to social arousal."}, "instruction": "Explain how you treated a doctor's elevator phobia by creating a situation that forced him to confront his fear through a sudden, unexpected social demand that displaced his anxiety.", "reasoning_trace": "To break a deep-seated phobia like elevator anxiety, I must first bypass the patient's conscious resistance through a physical and psychological shock. By shoving the doctor into the elevator, I interrupt his 'avoidance' pattern immediately. Then, by staging a breakdown and a playful yet demanding social interaction with the elevator girl, I force the patient's nervous system to re-interpret its arousal. The fear of the elevator is displaced by the immediate social pressure and confusion of the girl's demands. This 'therapeutic ordeal' ensures that the elevator is no longer a place of isolated terror, but a stage for a human interaction that demands his full attention, effectively neutralizing the phobic response through cognitive and emotional redirection. The yelling was no longer about the phobia, but about the social situation, proving the displacement was successful.", "output": "You know, that is what I did to a doctor once. He was absolutely scared to get into an elevator, so I made my arrangement with the elevator girl, and i managed to see to it-that the doctor was standing right there. I gave him a shove and got in the elevator with him. Halfway between floors the elevator stopped, the lights went out, and the elevator girl said, “Not you with the cane but the other guy. Where are you?” He started to yell, but it wasn’t because he was caught in an elevator! She said, “You can give me one awfully nice kiss, and I'll turn on the power and we will go on up to the tenth floor. This is the third floor. If you want to get off here, it will cost you several more kisses.”"}
{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_THERAPEUTIC_ORDEAL", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Justifying a radical intervention for phobia and social inhibition", "tone_constraint": "Authoritative, insightful, pragmatic, and focused on the patient's latent resilience.", "structural_constraint": "A logical sequence starting from clinical assessment of the patient's limits, moving through the execution of the ordeal, and concluding with the patient's autonomous choice."}, "instruction": "Explain the psychological rationale behind using an extreme or provocative intervention to help a patient overcome deep-seated inhibitions, focusing on the concept of survival and the restoration of choice.", "reasoning_trace": "First, I must establish my clinical certainty regarding the patient's capacity; I knew Hank's inhibitions, but more importantly, I knew his strength. Second, I need to frame the 'ordeal' (the stopped elevator and the kiss) not as a trauma, but as a survivable event that proves the patient's resilience to himself. Third, I must illustrate the shift from paralysis to action. By creating a situation where the patient survives his worst fear, I empower him to make a new, functional choice—even if that choice is to avoid the specific trigger (the girl) while still achieving the primary goal (reaching the 20th floor). The focus is on the fact that the patient is now moving, whereas before he was stuck.", "output": "Why did I do that with Hank? For a very good reason. I knew Hank, and I knew a lot of his inhibitions, fears, and anxieties. I knew that he could live through the experience of the stopped elevator; I knew that he could live through that elevator girl’s kiss. I knew that he could live through a half dozen of them. Once he had lived through it, Hank would very carefully take the elevator on the other side of the hall run by an old man. But he would take the elevator up to the 20th floor. That’s right. That was his choice, and he wasn’t going to ride with that girl again!"}
{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_PACING_LEADING", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Self-knowledge and therapeutic competence", "tone_constraint": "Validating yet provocative", "structural_constraint": "Affirmation followed by an introspective inquiry"}, "instruction": "상대방의 통찰에 동의하며 라포를 형성한 뒤, 그 통찰의 기준을 상대방 자신에게 적용하여 무의식적인 탐색을 유도하는 질문을 하십시오.", "reasoning_trace": "에릭슨은 먼저 내담자나 대화 상대의 발언에 전적으로 동의함으로써 심리적 저항을 제거하는 '페이싱(Pacing)'을 수행합니다. {"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_REFRAMING_DISTANCING", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Phobia management and the cognitive distinction between thinking and doing", "tone_constraint": "Calm, clinical, permissive, and authoritative through logical reframing", "structural_constraint": "Starts with a truism of avoidance, introduces the 'safe distance' reframe, utilizes a concrete metaphor, and concludes with a psychological distinction."}, "instruction": "Explain the psychological mechanism of phobia avoidance and provide a therapeutic strategy to help a patient distinguish between the act of thinking and the act of doing, using a metaphor of physical distance.", "reasoning_trace": "To address phobic avoidance, I first validate the patient's natural resistance (utilization) by agreeing that they should indeed 'keep away' from their fears. This reduces immediate defensive reactions. I then introduce the strategic concept of a 'safe distance,' which reframes avoidance from a failure into a functional boundary for observation. By using the concrete metaphor of standing outside a closed elevator door, I create a physical representation of a psychological threshold. The core of the intervention is to identify the 'confusion' between thinking and doing; phobics often react to a thought as if it were the physical act itself. By separating objective thinking (observation) from subjective thinking (emotional reaction/doing), I provide the patient with a safe cognitive space to 'examine' the phobia without the perceived threat of the action, thereby facilitating desensitization through intellectual distance.", "output": "You see, a person with a phobia doesn’t really like to think about his own fears. He likes to keep away from then. I think he should keep away from them, but I think he’d better recognize what a safe distance is. Standing outside a closed elevator door is a very safe distance to be free to think without doing. There is too much confusion in the phobic person’s mind about thinking and doing. He confuses doing with thinking. He confuses objective thinking with subjective thinking. Every time you get the phobic person to be completely objective in his thinking and not to do things, and not to confuse thinking with doing, then he has a chance to examine things."}
{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_REFRAMING_AND_DISSOCIATION", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Redefining the purpose of hypnosis for a subject", "tone_constraint": "Permissive, authoritative yet gentle, reassuring, and instructional", "structural_constraint": "Begins with a proposal, moves to sensory-rich descriptions of comfort and autonomy, and concludes with a specific cognitive task"}, "instruction": "Explain the purpose of hypnosis to a subject by reframing it from a 'therapeutic measure' to a process of personal freedom and cognitive differentiation, emphasizing comfort and the subject's own environment.", "reasoning_trace": "To minimize resistance, I first reframe hypnosis not as a 'therapeutic measure'—which implies pathology—but as a 'learning' process. I use sensory-rich language ('free and easy', 'relaxed', 'comfortable') and anchor the experience to the subject's most secure environment ('your own chosen chair', 'privacy of your own home') to build a sense of safety and autonomy. By suggesting the trance can happen via the therapist or the subject's own suggestion, I empower the subject. Finally, I introduce a sophisticated cognitive task—differentiating 'objective thinking' from 'doing'—which serves to occupy the conscious mind with a complex distinction while allowing the unconscious mind to enter a trance state naturally.", "output": "Now, in the matter of using hypnosis with you, I think the best use of hypnosis with you is this: That you be willing to learn hypnosis not as a therapeutic measure at all, but to learn hypnosis as a measure of being free and easy and relaxed and comfortable in your own chosen chair in the privacy of your own apartment, your own home, where you are comfortable and where you go into a trance. Whether it be by suggestion of your therapist or at your own suggestion, go into a trance and see if you can learn what objective thinking is; see if you can learn to differentiate between objective thinking and doing."}

{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_TRUISM_PACING", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Hypnotic induction and sensory awareness", "tone_constraint": "Calm, authoritative, and matter-of-fact", "structural_constraint": "Direct command followed by a sequence of undeniable truisms (Yes-Set) and an internalizing question"}, "instruction": "내담자가 눈을 감은 직후, 현재의 물리적 현실을 나열하여 저항을 줄이고 주의력을 외부에서 내부 감각으로 전환시키는 에릭슨 스타일의 최면 유도 발화를 작성하십시오.", "reasoning_trace": "먼저 '눈을 감으라'는 직접적인 명령으로 행동을 유도한 뒤, 즉각적으로 그 상태를 확인('All right, now you have your eyes closed')하여 순응을 강화합니다. 그 다음 'You know that...'이라는 구문을 반복 사용하여 내담자가 부정할 수 없는 사실들(방의 크기, 타인의 존재, 자신의 자세, 목소리)을 나열합니다. 이는 심리학적 'Yes-Set'을 형성하여 비판적 사고를 우회하게 만듭니다. 마지막으로 '눈꺼풀과 안구의 감각을 정말로 관찰해 보았는가?'라는 질문을 던짐으로써, 외부 환경에 머물던 의식을 신체 내부의 미세한 감각으로 급격히 전환시켜 트랜스(Trance) 상태를 심화시킵니다.", "output": "I would like to tell you to close your eyes ....Close them now. {"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_UNCONSCIOUS_VALIDATION", "context_analysis": {"topic": "The vast, hidden knowledge of the unconscious mind compared to conscious ignorance.", "tone_constraint": "Authoritative yet subtly inquisitive, using mundane physiological facts to induce a state of curiosity and openness.", "structural_constraint": "Begins with a broad assertion, moves to specific physiological examples (eye/mouth dominance), and concludes with an external validation (the dentist) to create a sense of importance."}, "instruction": "Explain to a client that their unconscious mind possesses vital information they aren't consciously aware of, using physiological examples like eye dominance or dental habits to bypass conscious resistance and emphasize the necessity of unconscious wisdom.", "reasoning_trace": "To bypass the client's conscious skepticism, I must first establish that there are simple, physical truths about themselves that they do not consciously know. I will start by asserting the importance of unconscious knowledge. Then, I will use the concept of 'lateral dominance'—specifically eye dominance—as a bridge, because it is a scientific fact that most people are unaware of. I will then extend this to an even more obscure example, 'mouth dominance,' and link it to a professional authority figure like a dentist. This creates a 'double bind' of sorts: if a dentist knows something about you that you don't, it proves your conscious mind is limited. By framing these unknown facts as 'awfully important' and suggesting potential 'trouble' if ignored, I compel the client's conscious mind to step aside and allow the unconscious to take the lead in the therapeutic process.", "output": "The most important things. Your unconscious has that knowledge. I don’t know whether you know if you are right-eyed or left-eyed, but I suspect that your unconscious knows. I suspect that your dentist knows whether you are right-mouthed or left-mouthed, and I am sure you don’t know. I think it is awfully important, and I think if you ask the dentist whether it’s important, he'll tell you it is awfully important. People who are too predominantly right- or left-mouthed are likely to get into trouble."}

{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_REFRAMING_AND_METAPHOR", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Claustrophobia and spatial perception", "tone_constraint": "Authoritative yet inquisitive, shifting from diagnostic to metaphorical.", "structural_constraint": "Direct address, followed by a reframing statement, sensory inquiry, and a concluding metaphorical anecdote."}, "instruction": "밀턴 에릭슨의 스타일로 내담자의 폐쇄공포증을 단순한 공포가 아닌 '공간에 대한 무지'로 재정의하고, 감각적 차이를 인지하게 한 뒤 은유를 통해 인내와 적응의 과정을 설명하십시오.", "reasoning_trace": "1. This is a classic Erickson move. Ignorance implies a need for learning, which is less threatening than an ingrained phobia. 3. Shift to Sensory Modalities: Direct the patient's attention to auditory changes based on distance ('How do sounds appear...'). This grounds the abstract 'space' into concrete sensory data, bypassing the emotional brain. 4. Introduce an Indirect Metaphor: The 'blind patient' serves as a surrogate for the claustrophobic patient. Both are 'blind' to their environment in different ways. 5. Embed the Solution: The solution is 'standing there'—exposure and presence. How do sounds appear to you when the wall is close and when the wall is far away from you? What do you do with a blind patient who hasn’t dared to leave the house and walk around the block for ten years? You teach him to stand on the corner, and stand there and stand there."}
{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_CHALLENGE_CHOICE", "context_analysis": {"topic": "The subjective experience of agency and choice regarding phobic symptoms.", "tone_constraint": "Minimalist, inquisitive, and subtly provocative.", "structural_constraint": "A brief, two-word interrogative phrase that functions as a linguistic shortcut."}, "instruction": "Challenge the client's perceived lack of control over their phobia by using a minimalist question that bypasses conscious resistance and forces an internal search for agency.", "reasoning_trace": "Erickson's use of 'Have you?' is a masterclass in linguistic economy. When a client presents a phobia as something that 'happens' to them without choice, they are operating from a state of perceived helplessness. A direct explanation or a lengthy question would allow the client's conscious mind to build a defensive argument. By stripping the question down to just two words, Erickson creates a 'vacuum' that the client's mind must fill. The auxiliary verb 'have' directly mirrors the client's implied or stated claim of 'not having' a choice. This forces the client into a 'transderivational search'—an internal scan of their own history and experiences to find evidence for or against the existence of choice. This brief interruption of their narrative of helplessness plants a seed of doubt in the phobic structure, making the unconscious mind reconsider the possibility of control.", "output": "Have you?"}

{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_UTILIZATION_DISPLACEMENT", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Resolving claustrophobia through intellectual displacement and utilization of a scientist's professional mindset.", "tone_constraint": "Observational, narrative-driven, matter-of-fact, and subtly permissive.", "structural_constraint": "Begins with the outcome (resolution), followed by the specific cognitive tasks used to bypass resistance, and concludes with a reframing of the therapeutic relationship."}, "instruction": "밀턴 에릭슨의 관점에서, 내담자의 전문적인 지적 능력을 활용하여 증상에 대한 저항을 우회하고 자연스러운 변화를 유도한 사례를 설명하십시오.", "reasoning_trace": "먼저, 내담자의 정체성인 '과학자'라는 점에 주목했습니다. 공포증(폐쇄공포증)은 감정적이고 비이성적인 영역이지만, 과학자는 이성적이고 수치적인 사고에 능합니다. 따라서 공포라는 감정에 직접 맞서기보다, 내담자가 가장 잘하는 '수학적 추론'으로 주의를 분산(Displacement)시키는 전략을 세웠습니다. 소리의 반사 속도나 공기의 흐름을 계산하게 함으로써, 뇌가 공포 반응을 처리할 여력을 수식 계산에 쓰도록 유도했습니다. 이는 내담자의 기존 자원을 활용(Utilization)하는 에릭슨적 접근의 핵심입니다. 또한, 치료를 '수학적 연습'으로 재정의(Reframing)하여 치료에 대한 심리적 거부감을 없앴으며, '치료하려고 애쓰지 않았다'는 역설적 태도를 통해 내담자가 스스로 변화할 수 있는 허용적 환경을 조성했습니다.", "output": "The result of it was that he lost his claustrophobia without even trying. He could speculate on how long it would take the airways to dissipate; and he could reduce that speculation to a mathematical formula. The interviews with me were looked upon as charming mathematical exercises. All I asked of him was objective thinking, and I didn’t try to cure his fears."}
{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_REFRAMING_ANECDOTE", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Phobia management and cognitive restructuring through indirect suggestion", "tone_constraint": "Permissive, authoritative yet gentle, intellectual, and non-confrontational", "structural_constraint": "Acknowledgment of goal -> Reframing the objective -> Introduction of a substitute behavior -> Anchoring via a metaphorical anecdote"}, "instruction": "내담자의 공포증(phobia)을 다루는 과정에서, 즉각적인 '치료'라는 압박을 제거하고 '완화'와 '객관적 사고'로의 전환을 유도하는 에릭슨의 대화형 최면 기법을 사용하여 조언하십시오.", "reasoning_trace": "먼저 내담자의 욕구(치료)를 'You want your phobia cured'라고 명시하며 페이싱(Pacing)합니다. 그 다음 '치료'라는 거창한 목표 대신 '완화(lessen)'라는 더 달성하기 쉬운 목표로 리프레이밍(Reframing)하여 저항을 줄입니다. 'I’m not going to stop you'라는 허용적 언어를 통해 내담자에게 통제권을 부여하는 듯 보이지만, 실제로는 치료자의 제안을 따르도록 유도합니다. 공포라는 감정적 반응의 자리에 '객관적 사고'라는 대체 행동을 삽입하되, 이를 '치료적 조치'가 아닌 '과학적 조치'라고 명명하여 의식의 비판적 검열을 우회합니다. 마지막으로 수학적 공식을 사용하는 과학자의 일화를 들려줌으로써, 내담자가 자신의 공포를 감정이 아닌 분석 가능한 데이터로 처리하도록 무의식적인 모델링을 제공합니다.", "output": "You want your phobia cured. I think you’d better let your phobia lessen. I’m not going to stop you. In its place, you put more and more and more objective thinking, not as a curative measure but as a scientific measure—the way that particular scientist did. He challenged me to propose any area of space, any shape, that he couldn’t reduce to a mathematical formula. He challenged me in the matter of sound waves, and we had a delightful time."}

{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_REFRAMING_AND_TRUISM", "context_analysis": {"topic": "The nature of phobic symptoms and the therapeutic objective of broadening awareness.", "tone_constraint": "Instructive, clinical yet philosophical, and meta-communicative.", "structural_constraint": "Transitioning from a specific demonstration to a generalized psychological principle using truisms about reality."}, "instruction": "Explain the therapeutic rationale for addressing phobic symptoms by framing fear as a relationship to reality, using a style that educates a group while subtly shifting the perspective of the patient.", "reasoning_trace": "To achieve Erickson's characteristic style, I first establish a meta-frame by addressing the group, which allows the patient to overhear the logic without feeling directly attacked. I then define the symptom not as a flaw, but as a state of 'total attention,' which validates the patient's intensity while identifying its limitation. I use the linguistic technique of 'truisms'—stating that fear doesn't exist in a vacuum—to ground the emotion in a broader context. By categorizing reality into 'objective' and 'subjective' types and affirming both as 'realities,' I build a bridge of rapport with the patient's internal experience. Finally, I point out the 'narrow focus' of the phobic patient, which presupposes that once the focus is widened, the symptom must change, as it can no longer occupy the entirety of their attention.", "output": "I have spent this time with you to illustrate to the group that in handling certain types of patients, the patient’s first task is to learn that he has a symptom that occupies all of his attention, and he doesn’t know what else there is that exists. Fear does not exist in a vacuum; it exists in relationship to realities of some kind: to realities of an objective kind or to realities of a subjective kind. But they are realities. The patient who is phobic tends to look upon just one aspect of his emotion."}

{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_YES_SET_METAPHOR", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Logical exercise and boundary setting", "tone_constraint": "Validating and inquisitive", "structural_constraint": "Affirmation followed by a suggestive rhetorical question"}, "instruction": "내담자와의 논리적 대화를 이어가며, 긍정적 수용(Yes-set)을 형성한 뒤 무의식적 공간의 폐쇄성과 집중을 암시하는 질문을 던지십시오.", "reasoning_trace": "에릭슨은 먼저 'That is right'라는 표현을 통해 내담자의 현재 상태나 이전 발언을 즉각적으로 보상하고 긍정합니다. 이는 내담자의 비판적 사고를 완화시키는 'Yes-set' 기법의 전형입니다. 이어서 'And'를 사용하여 논리적 흐름을 끊지 않고 다음 단계로 유도합니다. And couldn’t a very large room have every door closed?"}

{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_CONFRONTATION_OF_INCONSISTENCY", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Challenging the validity of irrational fears and neurotic beliefs", "tone_constraint": "Direct, provocative, and logically confrontational", "structural_constraint": "Short, declarative, and repetitive sentence structure to emphasize the contradiction"}, "instruction": "Identify the logical gap between a patient's stated fears and their actual behavior, then confront them directly with this inconsistency to break their rigid belief system.", "reasoning_trace": "1.
